Some frogs and toads inflate themselves to make themselves look large and fierce, and some spadefoot toads (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pelobates" title="Pelobates">Pelobates</a> spp</i>) scream and leap towards the attacker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collins_45-6"><a href="#cite_note-Collins-45">[45]</a></sup> Giant salamanders of the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Andrias" title="Andrias">Andrias</a></i>, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceratophryinae" title="Ceratophryinae">Ceratophrine</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pyxicephalus" title="Pyxicephalus">Pyxicephalus</a></i> frogs possess sharp teeth and are capable of drawing blood with a defensive bite. The <a href="/wiki/Blackbelly_salamander" title="Blackbelly salamander">blackbelly salamander</a> (<i>Desmognathus quadramaculatus</i>) can bite an attacking common garter snake (<i>Thamnophis sirtalis</i>) two or three times its size on the head and often manages to escape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cognition">Cognition</span></h2>
<p>In amphibians, there is evidence of <a href="/wiki/Habituation" title="Habituation">habituation</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associative_learning" title="Associative learning">associative learning</a> through both <a href="/wiki/Classical_conditioning" title="Classical conditioning">classical</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Instrumental_learning" title="Instrumental learning">instrumental learning</a>, and discrimination abilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>In one experiment, when offered live fruit flies (<i><a href="/wiki/Drosophila" title="Drosophila">Drosophila</a> virilis</i>), salamanders chose the larger of 1 vs 2 and 2 vs 3. Frogs can distinguish between low numbers (1 vs 2, 2 vs 3, but not 3 vs 4) and large numbers (3 vs 6, 4 vs 8, but not 4 vs 6) of prey. This is irrespective of other characteristics, i.e. surface area, volume, weight and movement, although discrimination among large numbers may be based on surface area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stancher_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stancher-156">[156]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation">Conservation</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Decline_in_amphibian_populations" title="Decline in amphibian populations">Decline in amphibian populations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bufo_periglenes1.jpg"><img alt="Golden toad" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2385" data-file-width="3576" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Bufo_periglenes1.jpg/220px-Bufo_periglenes1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Bufo_periglenes1.jpg/330px-Bufo_periglenes1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Bufo_periglenes1.jpg/440px-Bufo_periglenes1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bufo_periglenes1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The extinct <a href="/wiki/Golden_toad" title="Golden toad">golden toad</a> (<i>Bufo periglenes</i>), last seen in 1989</div></div></div>
<p>Dramatic declines in amphibian populations, including population crashes and mass localized <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a>, have been noted since the late 1980s from locations all over the world, and amphibian declines are thus perceived to be one of the most critical threats to global <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">International Union for Conservation of Nature</a> (IUCN) reported stating that currently birds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> mammals, and amphibians extinction rates were at minimum 48 times greater than natural extinction rates—possibly 1,024 times higher. In 2006, there were believed to be 4,035 species of amphibians that depended on water at some stage during their life cycle. Of these, 1,356 (33.6%) were considered to be threatened and this figure is likely to be an underestimate because it excludes 1,427 species for which there was insufficient data to assess their status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> A number of causes are believed to be involved, including <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">habitat destruction</a> and modification, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Over-exploitation" title="Over-exploitation">over-exploitation</a>, pollution, <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">introduced species</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endocrine-disrupting_chemical" title="Endocrine-disrupting chemical">endocrine-disrupting pollutants</a>, destruction of the <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">ozone layer</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultraviolet_radiation" title="Ultraviolet radiation">ultraviolet radiation</a> has shown to be especially damaging to the skin, eyes, and eggs of amphibians), and diseases like <a href="/wiki/Chytridiomycosis" title="Chytridiomycosis">chytridiomycosis</a>. However, many of the causes of amphibian declines are still poorly understood, and are a topic of ongoing discussion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Israel_painted_frog.JPG"><img alt="Hula painted frog" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1073" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Israel_painted_frog.JPG/220px-Israel_painted_frog.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Israel_painted_frog.JPG/330px-Israel_painted_frog.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Israel_painted_frog.JPG/440px-Israel_painted_frog.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Israel_painted_frog.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Hula_painted_frog" title="Hula painted frog">Hula painted frog</a> (<i>Discoglossus nigriventer</i>) was believed to be extinct but was rediscovered in 2011.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_webs_and_predation">Food webs and predation</span></h3>
<p>Any decline in amphibian numbers will affect the patterns of predation. The loss of carnivorous species near the top of the food chain will upset the delicate ecosystem balance and may cause dramatic increases in opportunistic species.
</p><p>Predators that feed on amphibians are affected by their decline. The <a href="/wiki/Western_terrestrial_garter_snake" title="Western terrestrial garter snake">western terrestrial garter snake</a> (<i>Thamnophis elegans</i>) in California is largely aquatic and depends heavily on two species of frog that are decreasing in numbers, the <a href="/wiki/Yosemite_toad" title="Yosemite toad">Yosemite toad</a> (<i>Bufo canorus</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_yellow-legged_frog" title="Mountain yellow-legged frog">mountain yellow-legged frog</a> (<i>Rana muscosa</i>), putting the snake's future at risk. If the snake were to become scarce, this would affect birds of prey and other predators that feed on it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Meanwhile, in the ponds and lakes, fewer frogs means fewer tadpoles. These normally play an important role in controlling the growth of algae and also forage on <a href="/wiki/Detritus" title="Detritus">detritus</a> that accumulates as sediment on the bottom. A reduction in the number of tadpoles may lead to an overgrowth of algae, resulting in depletion of oxygen in the water when the algae later die and decompose. Aquatic invertebrates and fish might then die and there would be unpredictable ecological consequences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStebbinsCohen1995249_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStebbinsCohen1995249-162">[162]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollution_and_pesticides">Pollution and pesticides</span></h3>
<p>The decline in amphibian and reptile populations has led to an awareness of the effects of pesticides on reptiles and amphibians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-163">[163]</a></sup> In the past, the argument that amphibians or reptiles were more susceptible to any <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemical" title="Chemical">chemical</a> contamination than any land aquatic vertebrate was not supported by research until recently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-163">[163]</a></sup> Amphibians and reptiles have complex life cycles, live in different <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecological" title="Ecological">ecological</a> zones, and are more vulnerable to chemical exposure. Certain pesticides, such as organophosphates, neonicotinoids, and carbamates, react via cholinesterase inhibition. Cholinesterase is an enzyme that causes the hydrolysis of acetylcholine, an excitatory neurotransmitter that is abundant in the nervous system. AChE inhibitors are either reversible or irreversible, and carbamates are safer than organophosphorus insecticides, which are more likely to cause cholinergic poisoning. Reptile exposure to an AChE inhibitory pesticide may result in disruption of neural function in reptiles. The buildup of these inhibitory effects on motor performance, such as food consumption and other activities.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation_and_protection_strategies">Conservation and protection strategies</span></h3>
<p>The Amphibian Specialist Group of the IUCN is spearheading efforts to implement a comprehensive global strategy for amphibian conservation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmphibianArk_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-AmphibianArk-164">[164]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amphibian_Ark" title="Amphibian Ark">Amphibian Ark</a> is an organization that was formed to implement the ex-situ conservation recommendations of this plan, and they have been working with zoos and aquaria around the world, encouraging them to create assurance colonies of threatened amphibians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmphibianArk_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-AmphibianArk-164">[164]</a></sup> One such project is the Panama Amphibian Rescue and Conservation Project that built on existing conservation efforts in Panama to create a country-wide response to the threat of chytridiomycosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup>
</p><p>Another measure would be to stop exploitation of frogs for human consumption. In the Middle East, a growing appetite for eating frog legs and the consequent gathering of them for food was already linked to an increase in <a href="/wiki/Mosquito" title="Mosquito">mosquitoes</a> and thus has direct consequences for human health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>
